<span id="freeTextContainer1067453735303197170">Peace may finally be at hand in the Middle East -- as Jack Ryan lays the groundwork for a plan that could end centuries of conflict.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText1067453735303197170">Peace may finally be at hand in the Middle East -- as Jack Ryan lays the groundwork for a plan that could end centuries of conflict. But ruthless terrorists have a final, desperate card to play; with one terrible act, distrust mounts, forces collide, and the floundering U.S. president seems unable to cope with the crisis. <p> With the world on the verge of nuclear disaster, Ryan must frantically seek a solution -- before the chiefs of state lose control of themselves and the world.</p></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_132061327">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/132061327" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1846302-richard-wright" class="left imgcol" title="Richard Wright"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442503263p2/1846302.jpg" alt="Richard Wright" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/132061327?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 23, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1846302-richard-wright" class="user" title="Richard Wright">Richard Wright</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1001566.The_Sum_of_All_Fears" title="Paperback 9780006471165" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1846302-richard-wright?shelf=2010" class="actionLinkLite">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer132061327">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14380765563142014572">Oh thank God. Thank God it's over. I picked this up en route to Goa a few weeks ago, and I seem to have been reading it forever. As always, Clancy's world is incredibly detailed and credible, in many ways all the more impressive for its sometime parallels to the world we live in today. As ever, the central plot is great. As ever, there's just too bloody much detail for anybody outside of the military to maintain much interest. The characters are for the most part the same seven or eight core peo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14380765563142014572">Oh thank God. Thank God it's over. I picked this up en route to Goa a few weeks ago, and I seem to have been reading it forever. As always, Clancy's world is incredibly detailed and credible, in many ways all the more impressive for its sometime parallels to the world we live in today. As ever, the central plot is great. As ever, there's just too bloody much detail for anybody outside of the military to maintain much interest. The characters are for the most part the same seven or eight core people, given different names and accents, and recycled at whim into a cast of thousands. The thousands are too many to keep track of. The detail of what they're doing is too monotonous and minuscule to do anything but slow the plot. And while the writing is functional, watch the inelegance of his point of view switches, requiring only a new paragraph to instigate, making it occasionally an act of backtracking and deduction to work out whose thoughts you're trying to follow. There's a good story buried in here, but it's splashed over so pointlessly large a canvas as to require almost forensic reconstruction to be able to see it.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14380765563142014572">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_400736830">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400736830" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/8480289-darren-burton" class="left imgcol" title="Darren Burton"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1349634688p2/8480289.jpg" alt="Darren Burton" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/400736830?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 07, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8480289-darren-burton" class="user" title="Darren Burton">Darren Burton</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer400736830">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6929898446201669050">It has been rumored that permission to publish this book had to go all the way to the U.S. Supreme Court and ever since then there is a standing court order that the CIA, FBI, and NSA receive advance copies of every Tom Clancy book a month before it goes to the publisher. Why? Well this book tells you step by step, in layman's language, in exacting detail how you build a hydrogen bomb. About the only thing that is left out is the exact amount of plutonium you would need. This did not sit well wi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6929898446201669050">It has been rumored that permission to publish this book had to go all the way to the U.S. Supreme Court and ever since then there is a standing court order that the CIA, FBI, and NSA receive advance copies of every Tom Clancy book a month before it goes to the publisher. Why? Well this book tells you step by step, in layman's language, in exacting detail how you build a hydrogen bomb. About the only thing that is left out is the exact amount of plutonium you would need. This did not sit well with the powers that be and considered it to be an extreme threat to national security. Clancy's lawyers pointed out that all of this information is available to the general public in any college library if someone is willing to take the time to look it up. The court agreed and allowed the book to be published without any of the information being removed.<br /><br />The story starts during the 1967 Arab-Israeli war. By then Israel had already secretly developed atomic weapons. Israel had a jet fighter loaded with an atomic bomb ready to scramble, the atomic bomb was not armed, but the plane was scrambled to go engage a group of tanks threatening the air base with the atomic bomb still attached. During the battle the plane was straffed with 50 caliber machine gun fire and the bomb mounts were hit, the bomb broke loose and came down in a farmers field. The jet crashed before it could limp home and the pilot was killed. Searches failed to locate the bomb. Flashforward, to the fall of the Berlin Wall. Communist scientists desperate for money sell detronium or "heavy water" to the palistinian terrorists allowing them to convert the atomic bomb to a hydrogen bomb. They decide that the Super Bowl will be the perfect target - since it is televised and the Vice Presedent of the United States has box tickets.<br /><br />You will be hanging by the edge of you seat waiting to see if they succeed.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6929898446201669050">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_30723198">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/30723198" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1413439-stephen" class="left imgcol" title="Stephen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" alt="Stephen" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/30723198?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 20, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1413439-stephen" class="user" title="Stephen">Stephen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer30723198">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14903885966832513898">3.0 to 3.5 stars. I am a big fan of Tom Clancy, especially of his characters Jack Ryan and John Clark, both of whom figure prominently in this Middle East thriller centering on Nuclear proliferation. As good as Clancy is and as compelling as the story can be, this one felt just TOO LONG to rate any higher. With some strategic editing, this one could have been amazing. As it is, it is still very good. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_253572676">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253572676" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2947350-jess" class="left imgcol" title="Jess"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Jess" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/253572676?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 23, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2947350-jess" class="user" title="Jess">Jess</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer253572676">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14509188916442568198">I finally got interested at about 600 pages - no kidding - for about 75 pages. <br /><br />This was the worst book I've ever read (there've been some other bad ones, but I had the common sense not to finish them). If I could take stars AWAY from a book, I would. At about 700 pages, it got so tedious that I thought I wouldn't finish; why was I wasting my time? (I had this thought a number of times while plowing through it.) After that, I was saying, 'Oh, come on!' because it became so outrageous. A better ti</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14509188916442568198">I finally got interested at about 600 pages - no kidding - for about 75 pages. <br /><br />This was the worst book I've ever read (there've been some other bad ones, but I had the common sense not to finish them). If I could take stars AWAY from a book, I would. At about 700 pages, it got so tedious that I thought I wouldn't finish; why was I wasting my time? (I had this thought a number of times while plowing through it.) After that, I was saying, 'Oh, come on!' because it became so outrageous. A better title would have been 'The Sum of All Ridiculousness'.<br /><br />A convoluted plot with numerous sub-plots that I just knew would come to a logical conclusion, instead came together in a contrived conclusion. and some didn't come together at all. There were sub-plots about Ryan, his wife, Caroline, who was called Cathy (don't ask me why) &amp; Dr. Ryan (as was Jack/Ryan/Dr. Ryan). Another sub-plot included President Fowler (Bob/Robert) &amp; Elizabeth/Liz/Dr. Elliot. There were high &amp; low level Arabs &amp; Russians, German military &amp; civilians, the U.S. Navy (submarine &amp; destroyer officers &amp; enlisted), Air Force (pilots &amp; Pentagon personnel, Israelis &amp; White House staff. Oh, &amp; the Japanese. They had a small part too. and the Mexicans. Have I missed anyone? Chinese? No, I don't think there were any mentioned.<br /><br />The sub-plots were confusing, but Clancy didn't think the story was complicated enough, so he spiced it up by referring to people, at various times, by their first names, last names, full names, nicknames, titles(multiple, &amp; sometimes just their informal roles), middle names, terms of endearment &amp; the reader was supposed to remember who he was talking about. Russian names? Forgetaboutit! I soon lost interest in keeping up with them (not just the Russians).<br /><br /><br />Several hundred pages, I'm sure, were spent describing the inner workings &amp; ingredients of bombs, submarines, aircraft, facilities for making them &amp; other dull stuff. Who cares? Dozens of pages were spent describing football plays &amp; players, which were background for the bombing, but really, dozens? An entire chapter was devoted to describing the inner workings of a bomb which fizzled.<br /><br />Goodley/Benjamin/Ben/Dr. Goodley was sent in by Dr. Elliot/Liz/Elizabeth to spy on &amp; sabotage Jack/Ryan/Dr. Ryan, then suddenly became his ally. What was with that?<br /><br />'Why did she finish this book at all?' you ask. At first I thought it would get better (not), then I felt I'd invested so much time in it I might as well finish, then I wanted to finish it so I'd have good cause for writing this scathing review.<br /><br />Tom Clancy is a pompous know-it-all (language cleaned up). I won't be reading another of his books.<br /><br />The almost five months spent reading this garbage were not entirely wasted. I read almost 30 other books concurrently with this one, most of which I enjoyed. I'm not exaggerating. I keep track of them on Goodreads.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14509188916442568198">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_357480857">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/357480857" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3181581-lisa" class="left imgcol" title="Lisa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442964571p2/3181581.jpg" alt="Lisa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/357480857?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 07, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3181581-lisa" class="user" title="Lisa">Lisa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer357480857">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9852416332565234709">This is a Tom Clancy novel where the movie is better than the book (like <em>The Hunt for Red October</em>). <em>The Sum of All Fears</em> is so crammed full of everything Tom Clancy learned about building a two-stage nuclear weapon and about submarines and submarine warfare that it really detracts from the interesting plot, which could have been pulled together in half or one third of the space. And if you haven't read earlier Clancy books you won't get some of the references to hero Jack Ryan's earlier adventur</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9852416332565234709">This is a Tom Clancy novel where the movie is better than the book (like <em>The Hunt for Red October</em>). <em>The Sum of All Fears</em> is so crammed full of everything Tom Clancy learned about building a two-stage nuclear weapon and about submarines and submarine warfare that it really detracts from the interesting plot, which could have been pulled together in half or one third of the space. And if you haven't read earlier Clancy books you won't get some of the references to hero Jack Ryan's earlier adventures, or to why there is so much animosity between him and NSA advisor Elizabeth Elliot. And that may prevent you from caring as much as you should about Ryan's imminent burn-out as Deputy Director of Central Intelligence. So see the movie on this one (reworked as a prequel before events in <em>The Hunt for Red October</em>). For something a little faster moving, try <em>Patriot Games</em>; for something where the endless set-up pays off much better (or for which I am more patient, since I am more interested in epidemiology than in nuclear weaponry), try <em>Executive Orders</em>. But you still may need to search for a "Cliff Notes" version of Ryan's earlier adventures to catch all the allusions and understand the nuances.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9852416332565234709">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_71588773">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71588773" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2723599-chad-sayban" class="left imgcol" title="Chad Sayban"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1333320931p2/2723599.jpg" alt="Chad Sayban" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/71588773?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 22, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2723599-chad-sayban" class="user" title="Chad Sayban">Chad Sayban</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/957388.The_Sum_of_All_Fears" title="Hardcover 9780399136153" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2723599-chad-sayban?shelf=highly-recommended" class="actionLinkLite">highly-recommended</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2723599-chad-sayban?shelf=own" class="actionLinkLite">own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2723599-chad-sayban?shelf=home-library" class="actionLinkLite">home-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer71588773">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3182543931438417044"><em>The Sum of All Fears</em> isn’t Tom Clancy’s best written book in the series, but as the title suggests, it is certainly the most frightening – especially when it was written during the collapse of the Soviet Union and the thaw of the Cold War. It is a sobering look at what can happen when dysfunctional Washington leadership is confronted with an unthinkable attack and how things can spiral out of control. Considering it was written ten years before 9/11, it is startling how it foreshadowed the worst</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3182543931438417044"><em>The Sum of All Fears</em> isn’t Tom Clancy’s best written book in the series, but as the title suggests, it is certainly the most frightening – especially when it was written during the collapse of the Soviet Union and the thaw of the Cold War. It is a sobering look at what can happen when dysfunctional Washington leadership is confronted with an unthinkable attack and how things can spiral out of control. Considering it was written ten years before 9/11, it is startling how it foreshadowed the worst frailties of leadership. <br /><br />It's not great art by any means, but it is intense storytelling and nobody works the details better than the techno-thriller master himself. More than any other book, I always wanted to see this one made into a movie - until the poor excuse for a movie was actually made. Now I wish my only memories were of the book. More than any of the Jack Ryan novels, the story of <em>The Sum of All Fears</em> sticks with me to this day.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3182543931438417044">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer40656321">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8176518843943922524">I'll do the same review for all Clancy's novels because they're all pretty much the same. Very long, very detailed, and after a while, very repetitive. If you stop after just a few of his books you'd probably give them 4 or 5 stars, but beyond that they start to grate. Especially where Jack Ryan is involved. I mean, Clancy spends hundreds of pages getting his details just right, the settings perfect etc., then he has Ryan dodging more bullets than James Bond! I finally threw my hands up and surr</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8176518843943922524">I'll do the same review for all Clancy's novels because they're all pretty much the same. Very long, very detailed, and after a while, very repetitive. If you stop after just a few of his books you'd probably give them 4 or 5 stars, but beyond that they start to grate. Especially where Jack Ryan is involved. I mean, Clancy spends hundreds of pages getting his details just right, the settings perfect etc., then he has Ryan dodging more bullets than James Bond! I finally threw my hands up and surrendered when Ryan becomes President. I can't remember what piece of crap that was in.<br /><br />I've given three stars as a compromise between my reactions when reading my first Clancy (brilliant) and last Clancy (doorstop).</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_197139247">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197139247" itemprop="url" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/197139247?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 10, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6010669-scott" class="user" title="Scott">Scott</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/415030.The_Sum_of_All_Fears" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780425133545" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6010669-scott?shelf=clancy" class="actionLinkLite">clancy</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer197139247">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9554221586470308882">Clancy's gripping depiction of just how fragile the nature of leadership can be in the midst of crisis is shockingly frightening. When emotions run high and the ever-present voice of reason (who else but Jack Ryan) is ignored, Clancy masterfully paints his most intense piece yet.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_325613240">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/325613240" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7672919-jerome" class="left imgcol" title="Jerome"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1330740421p2/7672919.jpg" alt="Jerome" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/325613240?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 07, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7672919-jerome" class="user" title="Jerome">Jerome</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer325613240">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1675569194790030854">While this book was not terrible, I found it much worse than other Clancy works. Clancy has always been a bit "long-winded," but I never noticed it quite like in The Sum of All Fears. Clancy's penchant for throwing endless trips to Carol Zimmer's store (and that annoying way he writes her accent), endless football banter between the "SecDef" and others, and other tedious paragraphs (he must have Marvin Russell fantasize about revenge for his brother's death at least 5 times - in nearly the exact</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1675569194790030854">While this book was not terrible, I found it much worse than other Clancy works. Clancy has always been a bit "long-winded," but I never noticed it quite like in The Sum of All Fears. Clancy's penchant for throwing endless trips to Carol Zimmer's store (and that annoying way he writes her accent), endless football banter between the "SecDef" and others, and other tedious paragraphs (he must have Marvin Russell fantasize about revenge for his brother's death at least 5 times - in nearly the exact same way - throughout the book) contribute extra pages to the book, and in the same way, takes away from pages that could be used to improve the book. This leads to my first complaint about the book.<br />The ending of The Sum of All Fears does not justify the nearly 800 hardcover pages that lead up to it. At all. It is quick (bang bang bang - and the book is over), and it simply does not do justice to the characters that are woven throughout the story. Furthermore, it is unclear. I don't want to give away anything, out of respect for a reader considering laboring through this enormous book, but when I turned the last page, I left quite unsatisfied. This ties in to my above theory: Clancy wastes so many valuable pages on meaningless tangents and the inclusion of too many details that he leaves himself without enough maneuvering room at the end to bring the book to a satisfying conclusion. Two examples: the whole Ricks USS Maine submarine tangent of the story is barely related to the plot of the book. It is merely thrown in to show us that Clancy knows submarines, I suppose; it wastes pages. Also, while impressive that Clancy did much research about how to build an H-Bomb, unless you are a budding third world terrorist/scientist, you might find yourself simply turning past the endless pages detailing H-Bomb construction.<br /><br />Next, besides Ryan and maybe Clark, Clancy cannot develop a character. Elliot, the NSA in the book, is a prime example. She hates Ryan, but we never know exactly why, other than she is a petty academic, without the real-world experience of Ryan. Perhaps that is enough, but that is a cliché, and it cheapens the book in that we never really know why the NSA has such a thing against the DDCI.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1675569194790030854">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_370256102">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/370256102" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4945739-hilmi-isa" class="left imgcol" title="Hilmi Isa"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1424434843p2/4945739.jpg" alt="Hilmi Isa" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/370256102?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 17, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4945739-hilmi-isa" class="user" title="Hilmi Isa">Hilmi Isa</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1001566.The_Sum_of_All_Fears" title="Paperback 9780006471165" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4945739-hilmi-isa?shelf=tom-clancy" class="actionLinkLite">tom-clancy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer370256102">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2894407551099581566">Segala-galanya bermula dengan satu peristiwa yang tidak dijangka dengan penemuan sebuah senjata nuklear yang tertimbus di dalam tanah pertanian milik seorang petani tua di Syria. Senjata itu merupakan sebuah bom nuklear milik Israel ketika Perang Arab-Israel 1973. Penemuan tersebut menyebabkan sebuah kumpulan pengganas Arab merancang untuk menggunakan senjata tersebut untuk menyerang Amerika Syarikat!<br />The Sum of All Fears merupakan novel ke-5 di dalam siri novel yang menampilkan Jack Ryan sebagai</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2894407551099581566">Segala-galanya bermula dengan satu peristiwa yang tidak dijangka dengan penemuan sebuah senjata nuklear yang tertimbus di dalam tanah pertanian milik seorang petani tua di Syria. Senjata itu merupakan sebuah bom nuklear milik Israel ketika Perang Arab-Israel 1973. Penemuan tersebut menyebabkan sebuah kumpulan pengganas Arab merancang untuk menggunakan senjata tersebut untuk menyerang Amerika Syarikat!<br />The Sum of All Fears merupakan novel ke-5 di dalam siri novel yang menampilkan Jack Ryan sebagai watak utama (juga dikenali sebagai Ryanverse). Di dalam novel kali ini,ditampilkan beberapa elemen baharu yang tidak terdapat di dalam novel-novel yang sebelumnya. Pada hemat saya,elemen-elemen ini merupakan daya penarik utama novel ini. Terdapat dua elemen yang didapati iaitu:<br /><br />a) Konflik antara watak-watak - Pada novel kali ini,penekanan diberikan kepada konflik hubungan antara Jack Ryan dan isterinya,Cathy Ryan. Selain itu,konflik antara Jack Ryan dan Elizabeth Elliot,Penasihat Keselamatan Kebangsaan kepada Presiden Amerika Syarikat,juga diketengahkan dan diperhalusi serta diangkat pada tahap yang baharu. Konflik ini sebenarnya sudah bermula sejak dari novel The Clear and The Present Danger. <br /><br />b) Adegan pertempuran tentera - Sebelum ini,walaupun terdapat babak-babak yang menggambarkan pertempuran antara dua buah tentera,tetapi ia dilakukan pada skala yang kecil. Pada novel kali ini,adegan pertempuran digambarkan agak besar yang melibatkan tentera darat,laut dan udara. <br /><br />Namun,malangnya,kedua-dua aspek di atas tidak diberikan perhatian yang benar-benar memuaskan dan mendalam. Sebaliknya,penulis lebih menumpukan perhatian kepada aspek-aspek teknikal dalam pembuatan bom nuklear. Penjelasan yang begitu teliti oleh penulis kadang-kala membosankan pembacaan saya. Malahan,saya berpendapat,terdapat beberapa situasi di mana penulis,Tom Clancy,boleh melakukan langkauan atau 'skip' untuk mengelakkan penjelasan yang terlalu panjang berjela dan membosankan.<br />Akibatnya,saya sedikit berasa kecewa pada novel ini. Malahan,saya terasa seolah-olah penulis agak tergesa-gesa menghabiskan penulisan novel ini. Oleh itu,saya hanya memberikan 3/5 bintang untuk novel ini pada kali ini. Pada asalnya saya ingin hanya memberikan 2 bintang sahaja. Namun,adegan-adegan aksi pada bab-bab akhir berjaya menyakinkan saya untuk menambah satu bintang lagi. Agak malang sebenarnya,kerana novel ini boleh menjadi novel yang lebih baik jika kelemahan yang saya nyatakan di atas diatasi.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2894407551099581566">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer52649585">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1646991485702143074"> The Sum of All Fears <br /> Tom Clancy<br /><br /> After the discovery of a damaged Israeli nuclear bomb which had gone missing in 1973, Arabs, who got their hands on this weapon of mass destruction, seek the help of a German scientist who helps them replicate the bomb in order for it to be used against the United States, after a treaty which is meant to settle the war against Israel and Arabians displeases them. <br /> As the engineering process of the weapon is complete, the Arabs, plan to use the weapon in a Super</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1646991485702143074"> The Sum of All Fears <br /> Tom Clancy<br /><br /> After the discovery of a damaged Israeli nuclear bomb which had gone missing in 1973, Arabs, who got their hands on this weapon of mass destruction, seek the help of a German scientist who helps them replicate the bomb in order for it to be used against the United States, after a treaty which is meant to settle the war against Israel and Arabians displeases them. <br /> As the engineering process of the weapon is complete, the Arabs, plan to use the weapon in a Super Bowl game in Denver, where hundreds of thousands of people will be killed, and will start a nuclear war between the United States and Russia, since suspicion always arouses on the largest competitor. <br /> Its up to DDCI Jack Ryan to uncover the most threatening terrorist acts of all time, and stop this crisis from occurring, or else, a third world war will begin. The Americans suspect the Russians for this act of terrorism. The Russians deny any involvement in the whole affair, however, the situation calls for immediate inquiry. Jack already has enough on his head, but he must also save his marriage, as well as save himself physically. <br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_31155057">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/31155057" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1266077-stephen-gallup" class="left imgcol" title="Stephen Gallup"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1321228329p2/1266077.jpg" alt="Stephen Gallup" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/31155057?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 29, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1266077-stephen-gallup" class="user" title="Stephen Gallup">Stephen Gallup</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer31155057">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17053495456544429974">I first heard of Tom Clancy in 1990, when a coworker told me about this author who'd become the darling of military specialists (sonar guys on submarines, for example) because his books displayed an in-depth understanding of their work.<br /><br />So I read <em>The Hunt for Red October</em>, which was fairly satisfying, and <em>Red Storm Rising</em>, after which I was pretty much Clancy-ed out for a while.<br /><br />After all, these are fairly hefty books, and with all those pages I'd prefer to see more character development. In <em>The Be</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17053495456544429974">I first heard of Tom Clancy in 1990, when a coworker told me about this author who'd become the darling of military specialists (sonar guys on submarines, for example) because his books displayed an in-depth understanding of their work.<br /><br />So I read <em>The Hunt for Red October</em>, which was fairly satisfying, and <em>Red Storm Rising</em>, after which I was pretty much Clancy-ed out for a while.<br /><br />After all, these are fairly hefty books, and with all those pages I'd prefer to see more character development. In <em>The Bear and the Dragon</em>, which I've subsequently heard on audio tape while driving, the characters tend to be mere caricatures or puppets.<br /><br />I think Clancy is a writer who is much improved when others process his stories to enhance the drama and trim out most of the esoterica. For example, to my recollection <em>Red October</em> is at least as good in movie form as in print. Also, the two Harrison Ford movies (<em>Patriot Games</em> and <em>Clear and Present Danger</em>) work fine as thrillers. I have no desire to check the originals to see how much other stuff was deleted. The John Ryan character in the books is highly unlikely to have the depth that Ford brings to the role.<br /><br />Anyway, more recently I came into possession of a well-worn copy of <em>The Sum of All Fears</em>, and knowing what I'd likely find, I approached it reluctantly. True to form, the paperback is over 900 pages long, and before getting far into it I knew it could easily have been boiled down to half that. The reader has to accept frequent jumps as the author weaves in a seemingly infinite number of story lines and a vast procession of characters, some of whom never reappear, and trust that eventually coherence will emerge.<br /><br />And, of course, it does. To simplify things drastically, we have (a) disaffected terrorists who are in possession of a nuclear bomb that they plan to use in order to spoil the world’s post-Cold War rush to peace and (b) incompetent politicians and government bureaucrats who are preoccupied with enhancing their careers and ruining the career of John Ryan. If these latter are the good guys, one might almost root for the terrorists. Well, not really, since the ultimate losers would be (or rather, are) thousands of innocent civilians.<br /><br />I didn't identify the perspective that makes the book worthwhile until page 306:<br /><br />"'You know what's the hard part of recognizing the truth?'" Jack asked. <br />'What’s that?' <br />'Knowing that something just bit you on the ass.'"<br /><br />By that point in the narrative, the terrorists have already shied away from recognizing the obvious -- that facts prove they have always been wrong and are still on the wrong side of history. And in the pages that follow we see the same willful blindness on the part of numerous highly placed people in Washington. After the terrorists do their work, creating a nightmare of confusion that foreshadows the real events of 9/11, panic-striken officials continue to act on the basis of poorly thought-out assumptions. In other words, the real story is about the drive people have to find fault with others and their resistance to consider the possibility of being wrong themselves. Ryan spells this out for a neophyte on page 452: <br /><br />"'I am not always right. I make mistakes. But I am smart enough to know that, and because I'm that smart, I look for people with opposing views to backstop me. That's a good habit to get into. ... If you can prove to me that you are no more a prisoner of your views than I try to be of mine, then you have a future here. Objectivity isn't easy. You have to exercise it.'"<br /><br />Clancy redeems himself at such points, but this story has the same flaws as the others. It's far from being great fiction. (Particularly bad is the part where Ryan's wife suspects him of infidelity and then has a cat fight with the hussy who'd made her doubt her man.) However, in the years since this was written, the human failing demonstrated here has become far more obvious to me in America's increasingly polarized society. It's much more satisfying for us to demonize the other side (i.e., whichever political party we happen to hate) than to consider the admittedly slim possibility that we might be going off half-cocked.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17053495456544429974">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer62616894">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8194191122817466940">This book is full of action, from start to finish. It is also an interesting look at how American politics might work. The big takeaway, I think, is that you don't have to be a powerful nation to build a hydrogen bomb, and it wouldn't be that difficult to get such a bomb across our borders.<br /><br />Although I don't foresee complete disarmament of the worlds nukes any time soon, the idea that these devices should not exist, even in the hands of world leaders, is compelling. How can even the President of t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8194191122817466940">This book is full of action, from start to finish. It is also an interesting look at how American politics might work. The big takeaway, I think, is that you don't have to be a powerful nation to build a hydrogen bomb, and it wouldn't be that difficult to get such a bomb across our borders.<br /><br />Although I don't foresee complete disarmament of the worlds nukes any time soon, the idea that these devices should not exist, even in the hands of world leaders, is compelling. How can even the President of the U.S. feel it is right to use weapons of mass destruction, which inevitably would kill men, women, and children? This book presents a scenario of how even good government leaders could let a situation escalate to the point of nuclear holocaust.<br /><br />This was a really long book. I think it could have been shorter. The first half of the book, which focused on a treaty for peace in Palestine, almost seemed like it belonged in another book. It's really two good books wrapped into one.<br /><br />I recommend this book for adults who like a lot of action, politics, submarines, and technology. There is some strong language, and a little adult subject matter (not explicit).</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8194191122817466940">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13061765757908072308">This book was very exciting, just like the film, but more. It starts off with a protest gone wrong in Israeli. Palestinians begin to use peaceful protests but a protestor is killed and therefore, U.S. cannot support Israel. But U.S. manages to resolve the situation and create long lasting peace. However,there is a group of Muslim terrorists who are looking at this lasting peace as a failure in their campain for their anger is toward the U.S. They retaliate by detonating a bomb in a stadium located in Colorado. The results are devastating and the plan is thwarted by Jack Ryan who proves with evidence that bomb in fact came from the U.S. I love how the author uses these events and makes it incredibly fast paced. You have to keep up with everything that is going on, with the terrorists and those trying to diffuse the situation. The author uses advanced vocabulary and many characters which is interesting because you can see it from many points of view. I enjoyed this book very much.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9100846930606425914">I just re-read this book (about 15 or so years after reading it the first time), and I need to warn those who are thinking of reading it or who have just begun: stick with it through all the different story lines! Make notes if you have to, but Clancy doesn't tell you something that isn't going to come into play in the story later. Also, it may seem to go slowly for the first half of the book (which is a big book, admittedly), the second half of the book is nearly continual action and drama.<br /><br />Basi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9100846930606425914">I just re-read this book (about 15 or so years after reading it the first time), and I need to warn those who are thinking of reading it or who have just begun: stick with it through all the different story lines! Make notes if you have to, but Clancy doesn't tell you something that isn't going to come into play in the story later. Also, it may seem to go slowly for the first half of the book (which is a big book, admittedly), the second half of the book is nearly continual action and drama.<br /><br />Basically, it's Clancy being Clancy, and it's absolutely outstanding, but if this is your first Clancy novel, I would recommend beginning with something less complex such as "The Hunt for Red October" or "Patriot Games" because this one has about 12 separate story lines - that's not an exaggeration; it may even be more than that! - and it gets complex quickly.<br /><br />If you make it through the first half of the novel, your reward is a great novel!</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_189457644">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer189457644">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18027503979562239414">Dear <em>Penthouse Letters</em>:<br /><br />You'll never believe what happened one day when I was sitting in the library, flipping through the latest copy of "Jane's Guide to Military Technology"--let's just say that my passive sonar went active! <br /><br />Ping-ping-ping went my heart at the thought of sturdily-designed hardware like the Israeli Merkava tank...the shaft of its 120mm MG253 smoothbore gun, capable of firing APDS as well as HEAT rounds looming over me, making me quiver...I couldn't help but imagine the feel of i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18027503979562239414">Dear <em>Penthouse Letters</em>:<br /><br />You'll never believe what happened one day when I was sitting in the library, flipping through the latest copy of "Jane's Guide to Military Technology"--let's just say that my passive sonar went active! <br /><br />Ping-ping-ping went my heart at the thought of sturdily-designed hardware like the Israeli Merkava tank...the shaft of its 120mm MG253 smoothbore gun, capable of firing APDS as well as HEAT rounds looming over me, making me quiver...I couldn't help but imagine the feel of its ceramic-steel-nickel alloy classified armor brushing ever so softly against my cheek, sending chills down my spine, yet stoking the fire that burns deep in my soul...<br /><br />Mystified in Maryland,<br /><br />Tom Clancy</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/530039163" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/12949855-corey-tardif" class="left imgcol" title="Corey Tardif"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1348008732p2/12949855.jpg" alt="Corey Tardif" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/530039163?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12949855-corey-tardif" class="user" title="Corey Tardif">Corey Tardif</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer530039163">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2312655277101663101">This probably has to be the biggest book by Tom Clancy I've read since Rainbow Six. While getting through the first couple of chapters, it was a little hard to follow, but as I read more, it started to make sense. The book was a lot better than the movie starring Ben Affleck, who played Jack Ryan, the movie was decent but the book was better, and also very different from the movie.<br /><br />There were parts in the book that my heart started racing because of the suspense, I literally couldn't put it down.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2312655277101663101">This probably has to be the biggest book by Tom Clancy I've read since Rainbow Six. While getting through the first couple of chapters, it was a little hard to follow, but as I read more, it started to make sense. The book was a lot better than the movie starring Ben Affleck, who played Jack Ryan, the movie was decent but the book was better, and also very different from the movie.<br /><br />There were parts in the book that my heart started racing because of the suspense, I literally couldn't put it down. Even though it was lengthy, it was definitely worth reading. Highly recommended to Tom Clancy fans!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2312655277101663101">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer315247705">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1256029156585810848">Undoubtedly the best Jack Ryan book, this novel follows the ever-more successful American intelligence guru as he struggles to uncover the plot of a terrorist cell. Clancy’s technical knowledge is impressive as always, but in this book he strikes home with very real and compelling characterizations of Ryan and his political opponents. The terrorist plot is bold, but not as bold as Clancy as he drops perhaps the biggest surprise twist in any of his books as the plot screams to a climax. In the po</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1256029156585810848">Undoubtedly the best Jack Ryan book, this novel follows the ever-more successful American intelligence guru as he struggles to uncover the plot of a terrorist cell. Clancy’s technical knowledge is impressive as always, but in this book he strikes home with very real and compelling characterizations of Ryan and his political opponents. The terrorist plot is bold, but not as bold as Clancy as he drops perhaps the biggest surprise twist in any of his books as the plot screams to a climax. In the post 9/11 world, The Sum of All Fears is a chilling tale of what could happen today.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1256029156585810848">...more</a>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16176293" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/852768-samuel" class="left imgcol" title="Samuel"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1315950321p2/852768.jpg" alt="Samuel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/16176293?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 23, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/852768-samuel" class="user" title="Samuel">Samuel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/415030.The_Sum_of_All_Fears" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780425133545" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Clancy fans, military buffs.</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/852768-samuel?shelf=mystery-suspense" class="actionLinkLite">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer16176293">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16212128749352415834">You have to like Clancy to like this. It takes a bit to get going and Clancy loves to go overboard in descriptives - "Amal stood on a cliff, formed in the jurassic period by pressure from volcanoes, he was holding an uzi, the metal for the uzi was mined in siberia by people who have low cholesterol b/c they eat a lot of salad...", I get it, Amal has a gun, move on! Despite that, he takes an all too real scenario and gives it legs, puts the thought in the back of your brain, and does a good job w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16212128749352415834">You have to like Clancy to like this. It takes a bit to get going and Clancy loves to go overboard in descriptives - "Amal stood on a cliff, formed in the jurassic period by pressure from volcanoes, he was holding an uzi, the metal for the uzi was mined in siberia by people who have low cholesterol b/c they eat a lot of salad...", I get it, Amal has a gun, move on! Despite that, he takes an all too real scenario and gives it legs, puts the thought in the back of your brain, and does a good job working through the characters and scenarios. Not a quick read.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16212128749352415834">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fka0NRV/68scy+VyVXZDLMtkG4THQIQ7LbD4l4j5tDYbkovm563/MZATkckrF6WegpPYnY6dw5FHuf0FRGxCcw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Rvw4WYWLKartcrwXzJXBBQzZoFV4KLd9FJjSS7UpFHgjKAeKd1k9UGGqyKyy9Ce3RS5jTDH18Nd+kdfZebziPQ==')})

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3892.Tom_Clancy">About Tom Clancy</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/3892.Tom_Clancy"><img alt="3892" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1407672935p2/3892.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer6764881982677131410">Tom Clancy was an English major at Baltimore’s Loyola College. As a Maryland insurance broker with a passion for naval history, his dream of writing a novel came true with his first effort, <em>The Hunt for Red October</em> (1984). <br /><br />He since wrote more than a dozen novels, which have a blend of realism and authenticity, intricate plotting, and razor-sharp suspense. Ten of the novels, including <em>The Teeth of</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6764881982677131410">Tom Clancy was an English major at Baltimore’s Loyola College. As a Maryland insurance broker with a passion for naval history, his dream of writing a novel came true with his first effort, <em>The Hunt for Red October</em> (1984). <br /><br />He since wrote more than a dozen novels, which have a blend of realism and authenticity, intricate plotting, and razor-sharp suspense. Ten of the novels, including <em>The Teeth of the Tiger</em> (Berkley, 2004), feature the character Jack Ryan, former stock broker and CIA employee. <br /><br />Clancy’s non-fiction works include a series of guided tours of America’s warfighting assets, Submarine, Armored Cav, Fighter Wing, Marine, and Airborne.<br /><br />He lived in Maryland.<br /><br />The following are the books and approximate time frame in the <em>Jack Ryan Universe</em><br /><br />Without Remorse		1969-73<br />Patriot Games			1981-82<br />Red Rabbit			1982<br />The Hunt for Red October	1984<br />The Cardinal of the Kremlin	1986<br />Clear and Present Danger	1988<br />The Sum of All Fears		1990-91<br />Debt of Honor			1995-96<br />Executive Orders		1996<br />Rainbow Six			1999-2000<br />The Bear and the Dragon	2002<br />The Teeth of the Tiger	2006<br />Dead or Alive			2007<br />Locked On			2007<br />Threat Vector			2009<br />Command Authority		2013<br />Support and Defend		2014<br />Full Force and Effect		2014</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6764881982677131410">...more</a>

    </div>

The oligarchs who support him expect a constant flow of graft, but with energy prices cratering, the Russian economy sputters to a virtual halt. Unable to grow the Russian market at home, his hold on power relies on expansion abroad—a plan that has been thwarted by the United States in the past.But this time Volodin has determined that an indirect approach is the best. A floating natural gas facility in Lithuania is blown up. A Venezuelan prosecutor is assassinated. A devastating attack on a Russian troop train kills dozens. A chaotic world is the best camouflage for a series of seemingly unrelated attacks.Only one man recognizes an ominous pattern in the reports of terror from around the globe. U.S. President Jack Ryan sees a guiding hand in the worldwide chaos, but before he can act he needs proof.While his intelligence agencies race to uncover the truth behind the attacks, the President struggles to unite a fractious and distrustful coalition of Western nations against the schemes of the Russian dictator.With five thousand Russian troops poised to invade a NATO nation, can Jack Ryan move swiftly enough to stop Volodin’s grand plan of global conflict and conquest?
